GT: -beta*sin(v) - mu*(c0 - x**c1)*v - omega0**c2*x*exp(-Abs(x))

I need to determine which candidates can exactly match the Ground Truth (GT):

$$GT = -0.194830767863936 \cdot v \cdot (1 - x^2) - 3.04923978373096 \cdot x \cdot \exp(-|x|) - 0.143047751034959 \cdot \sin(v)$$

Let me expand this:
$$GT = -0.19483v + 0.19483v \cdot x^2 - 3.04924 \cdot x \cdot e^{-|x|} - 0.14305 \cdot \sin(v)$$

The key basis functions in GT are:
1. **v** (linear in v)
2. **v┬Ęx┬▓** 
3. **x┬Ęexp(-|x|)** ŌĆö this is crucial and non-polynomial
4. **sin(v)** ŌĆö this is crucial

Now, let me analyze the candidates. Most candidates use combinations of:
- `tanh(c┬Ęx)` or `tanh(x)` ŌĆö these approximate `x┬Ęexp(-|x|)`? No, `tanh` is an odd function bounded between -1 and 1, while `x┬Ęexp(-|x|)` is also odd but has different shape. These are **not equivalent**.
- `x┬Ę|x|`, `x┬│`, `xŌüĄ` ŌĆö polynomial/piecewise polynomial terms
- `v┬Ę|v|`, `v┬│` ŌĆö these could approximate `sin(v)` but are **not equivalent**
- `v┬Ęx┬▓` ŌĆö matches one GT term
- `v` ŌĆö matches one GT term

**Critical observation:** The GT contains `x┬Ęexp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)`. None of the candidates contain `exp` or `sin` functions. 

Can `tanh(c┬Ęx)` equal `x┬Ęexp(-|x|)`? No ŌĆö `tanh` is monotonically increasing and bounded, while `x┬Ęexp(-|x|)` has a maximum at x=1 and decays to 0. They are fundamentally different functions.

Can any polynomial/piecewise combination of `v┬│`, `v┬Ę|v|`, `v` equal `sin(v)`? No ŌĆö `sin(v)` is periodic and bounded, while polynomials grow without bound.

Can `x┬Ę|x|` + `x┬│` + `xŌüĄ` + `tanh(c┬Ęx)` + `x` equal `x┬Ęexp(-|x|)` + linear terms in x? No ŌĆö the exponential decay cannot be replicated by polynomials or `tanh`.

Similarly, candidates with `x^c3` (like Candidates 2, 31, 48, 49, 50) or `Max(0,x)┬▓` don't help create `exp(-|x|)` or `sin(v)`.

Since **every single candidate** lacks both `exp(-|x|)` and `sin(v)` as basis functions, and these cannot be constructed from the available basis functions (polynomials, `tanh`, `|┬Ę|`, `Max`), **none of the candidates can match the GT**.
